< Review>
My husband and I took lessons with Christopher Li for our first dance. We signed up for twelve lessons, and we enjoyed every session with Chris.  He not only choreographed our first dance, but he choreographed another routine for us that we wanted to surprise our guest with.  This dance is called Marinera, a Peruvian coastal dance - a graceful, romantic couple dance that uses hanker-chiefs as props. Chris had no prior experience with this type of dance, but he did his research and delivered when teaching us our routine! We're so grateful for Chris. He really taught my husband how to lead, and taught us a lovely dance that our family and friends will always remember!< /Review>

<user_name>Olivia Hemenway<//user_name><time>1561326545400< /time><Rate>5< /Rate>< text>
My husband and I got married last summer and knew early into our wedding planning that we wanted to have a unique first dance. We had the song picked out and a vision of being surrounded by family and friends holding sparklers while the sun sets. Neither of us were confident enough to choreograph our own dance routine so we researched studios in the area we could take lessons at. We were so impressed after our complimentary consultation at Mark Ballas with Zach and Chris, we signed up for a private 10-lesson package.

We felt a little out of our comfort zone at first since we aren't the best dancers and had never done anything like this before, but our instructor Chris was very patient and encouraging with us. Other instructors that were in the studio at the same time would also watch our routine and offer motivation. Chris broke up the routine into manageable sections for us to easily learn while still having fun, and after 10 lessons we couldn't believe the progress we made and confidence we built.

I had high expectations for how our first dance would turn out, and they were far exceeded when we finally performed at our wedding. Not only was it easily one of the most memorable moments of the night, but the most memorable experience throughout our entire wedding planning process. Chris and the Mark Ballas team are talented, professional and friendly, and made us feel like part of their family. I highly recommend this studio for anyone looking to choreograph a one-of-a-kind first dance for their wedding as well!< /text>

< Text>
I can't say enough good things about the Mark Ballas Studio for ballroom dancing! Amazing instructors who all seem to be very passionate about what they do. They are quick to dance with beginners and are very encouraging. I went to a belated Valentine's  dance tonight and they put on a heck of a great, clean, fun party which is amazing in this day and age. They make sure people without partners get to dance. Their prices for lessons are very reasonable. I live in Livermore and could go to the Arthur Murray studio here but I choose to drive to Pleasanton several nights a week because of the quality I get at Mark Ballas.

Another thing I like is that instructors will dance together occasionally to demonstrate where you can get if you stick with it. For me, that gets me excited about my own possibilities on the dance floor. They talk about becoming part of their "dance family" and after only four times taking lessons and one party I honestly feel like I'm becoming part of it. That might sound corny but it's a tribute to how well all the staff, not just the instructors, reach out to folks.

On a logistics level, they have ample parking, greats dance floors (two different rooms), wonderful front desk staffing, are prompt to return calls, a great website, clean restrooms (even stocked with hand lotion, deodorant,  hairspray, etc.) and a level of enthusiasm that's hard to find in a service oriented business.

Can you tell I'm  sold on this place? I honestly can't currently think of even a suggestion I could give them on how to improve. Trust me, I'm not being paid to write this nor am I an employee, spouse, etc. I  NEVER, EVER write or have written a review like this about any business or service!!! I'm simply 20 star impressed about a 5 star situation. If you don't believe what I'm saying, come experience it yourself, first hand.

I feel totally stoked to have come across this place at a time in my life that has recently been full of unexpected change. Thank you Mark Ballas folks for being there right when I needed you! And thank all of you out there who have taken time to read this review. I haven't been this passionate about something in a long time!</Text>

<rate>5<//rate><Text>What can I say about this East Bay Dance Academy? Let me list the top 3 things in my mind and summarize why I think it is among the best places for not only dance instruction but an overall fun place to enjoy a social event. 1) Top-notch instruction: Clearly you must be excited to see world-class Instructors teaching the classes. Beginning or Intermediate levels. Privates too. All are taught by excellent Instructors. They surely can dance and technically have the understanding for the craft, but to be able to break it down into simplest forms, make it engaging and fun at same time, and offer progress and improvement on the student's part? Well this takes special teachers. I have taken 2 very different types of classes here. One was American Rumba and the other West Coast Swing. Both were fantastic. 2) Schedule of variety of dance classes: this is not your local gym or community center. It is a professional dance studio and academy really. I call it this to distinguish its intent. As far as my humble eye can see this place really wants to make a serious dancer more serious. A completely shy and introverted beginning dancer more open and confident. And a socially awkward but keenly interested in the art of dance type of student more capable than what s/he would initially believe. 3) Cool Vibe: C'mon now. Dancing is cool. It can be intimidating especially when done at a high level but it is just outright cool to do, watch, learn, socialize..etc. My background is a fitness and martial arts lover. I attend One World Jiu Jitsu in Newark and its affiliate AKA (American Kickboxing Academy) in Sunnyvale. I know the best of the best. No ego. Openness. Welcoming attitude to ALL. Unless you are a stinky bum off the streets you will be welcome. High caliber is humble and full of grace. I also was recently accepted into a Latin American focused dance company. But I auditioned out of passion and a love for it. Not so much experience at all because I had zero in terms of the specific dance style. Afro-Haitian-Cuban Salsa and also rumba. It is SF based so I commute but for East Bay I choose Mark Ballas. Just come try a class or drop in and observe first. I guarantee you will love it and be inspired to learn more. It only takes 1 good class (and they are all good here) to make you into a better dancer! In literature, legend and art; canaries have represented joy, hope and love. They were brought to Europe by Spanish sailors in the late 15th Century and from the 1700s, they have been pets, genetically distinct from their wild ancestors. <user_name>Jay Mills< /user_name><Time>1562009950830< /Time><rating>1</rating>< Text>
The absolute least welcoming most depressing bird store in San Diego . I enjoy visiting different bird stores since I've wanted a pet bird for ages but don't have the means to own one and this store was so dissapointing. I usually go to Feathered Friends or Free Flight(both great bird-loving establishments) but I was having dinner at Sorrentinos and had heard about this place and decided to check it out. Instant regret. It was a hot Sunday afternoon and this place was at least 10 degrees hotter inside.The smell of neglected bird cages hits immediately and overpriced product is the majority of the store. All the birds were all cramped against a wall in very dirty cages and they had 3 birds out on some cramped stands waaaay in the back. I was in this place for about 10 minutes before I had to walk out because of the smell and 90 degree heat and the only acknowledgment I got was from a blonde employee who kept giving me a look like she wanted me to stop interacting with the birds. Won't be back. Hope this place gets shut down by the proper authorities because the birds in there do not deserve to be living in such terrible conditions.<//Text>

<date>1593744574825<//date>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
<gmap_id>0x809c1e4608387c75:0xdf36a8a983ab8d1d</gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
<Pictures>None</Pictures>< Text>
The campground is nice but although the ramps are open, the dock is not in the water. And there are submerged rocks along the boat ramp which we hit and bent out prop. We had to take the boat out of the water.
We were told that we could not leave the boat and trailer in the parking lot at the boat launch, and that we had to park in the overflow parking for our campground. The problem is that they chopped down a bunch of trees and all the wood is piled up in the overflow so you can't park a boat there.
We decided to park behind a few other boats along a dirt road next to the overflow. There were no signs saying No Parking, and there were at least 3 other boats and vehicles parked on the same road.
We were there for the whole weekend with friends who also had a boat and when we got off the water that evening, we found a parking ticket for $280 on our boat!! There was nowhere else to park because the campground had taken the overflow to store wood. We were not blocking any road, they just want the revenue and assume we'll just pay the ticket.
If possible I will NEVER return to this campground.</Text>

Camped here since 1996, it was on a whim we found this lake back then. Spent many a summers here with my family and close friends.  The memories we made over the years we will cherish a few lifetimes over. < review>
Well kept camp grounds. (Doc) the camp grounds host is a friendly guy who lives there during the busy season is helpful and good source for local info. Stunning mountain setting and thanks to noise regulations in the grounds it's quiet at night. Star filled sky's and great fishing. My only complaint is, if you cook outdoors the yellow jackets are after your food. And they don't give up. Otherwise great place.<//review>

<review>Dirty environment. Last time I visited I couldn't help but be put off by the collection of filth under the equipment behind the register. While I witnessed employees doing there best to clean up spills they neglected to clean under the large metal equipment. I doubt their efforts could remove what looks like years of neglect. They'd probably have to replace the flooring to even remotely clean this area. Additionally the equipment the employees used looked filthy itself, concerning me over the true quality of cleanliness that their efforts could achieve in the areas they can reach to clean.

The place is always packed which surprises me as the quality of milk tea is lacking. I hear the chicken is good, but from what I've seen the product is nothing like what is advertised on the menu.

The boba itself is hit or miss, somedays it's perfect and others it's burnt. I'm not sure what they use in brewing the tea but I've become ill multiple times after consuming the product, once throwing up before I was able to leave the store having to run outside quickly to avoid causing another mess for the staff to clean.

My experience with the staff has been alright. They're often friendly. My order is usually what I place, except for one time in which a male staff member incorrectly prepared my order which I didn't notice till after I had already left.

With plenty of places in IV that have Boba I would absolutely recommend going elsewhere. The service is the only quality component at Wake Cup. < Text>
I read the reviews prior to going here, and the bad ones seem punitive for some reason that I could not discern.  I'm giving this place five stars because the Owners are troopers -- open for indoor dining currently -- and also because the food is quite tasty, and adequately proportioned, leaving room for dessert and coffee.  I had the eggplant burger, and I wanted to eat two of them, it was so delicious, but I was with a bunch of people and that would have been socially unacceptable.  I will be back!  There were lots of options for non-vegetarians, too.  It is the kind of place that you go to EAT in the afternoon.  Sit down and enjoy it.  You can eat a bunch of different, delightful things.  We had a party of 4, with the scrumptious artichoke heart appetizer, three entrees, and a bottle of fine wine, and the tab was $107.00.  I was impressed, and that is no easy feat.</Text>

After a really long day, all I wanted was a cup of coffee. Strangely, it seems like everywhere that serves coffee (except for the admirable Harmony Cafe) closes briefly before dinner. Well, after my experience at Harmony Cafe, it's evident that I should have foregone the coffee all together.

There was just one table dining already. The hostess was chatting with them when we arrived, and kindly removed herself from their conversation to greet us. She asked if we had a reservation; we didn't. She seated us, then returned shortly to take our order. Two cappuccinos.

Just a moment to comment on the cappuccinos themselves: I have had many cappuccinos from a great deal of places, and while these weren't bad and the price was average (~$5), I would say Starbucks‚Äîsurprisingly‚Äîdoes theirs better. No, really.

<Review>We were lured in for dinner by the simple but pleasant sounding menu and pianist. We ordered the chicken liver bruschetta as an appetiser to share - it was beautifully presented but let down by a lack of seasoning.

For entrees, I had the fish with fava beans, cherry tomatoes and garlic bread. Again, it was woefully under-seasoned. Once I had added salt, it was a little better but still not great. I also have a suspicion it was microwaved due to the blistering heat of the broth and the way in which The fish had shrunk,  but I may be wrong. The garlic bread was completely lacking in garlic - it was just bread.

My husband had the tagliatelle with sausage and peas, which he enjoyed but conceded that it was very basic and something we would make better at home.

I had my eye on the torta della nonna for dessert as it's one of my favourites  but I didn't bother ordering it as I knew it would just disappoint.

I'm genuinely surprised by the good reviews for this place - my father is Italian and a restaurateur (he is the head chef of his own restaurant) and so I have grown up eating simple but excellent Italian food; the menu here appealed to me for that very reason but it talked a good game and didn't live up to it.

For the standard of food, the menu is incredibly overpriced. We paid $100 (including tip as the waitress was very friendly and attentive) for an entree and two appetisers plus three drinks.

On the plus side, the music was wonderful.< /Review><resp>None</resp>< gmapID>
